polluted waters, except where suitable treatment has been provided in
accordance with subsequent provisions of this code;
   C.   Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be prohibited, and a public
offense, to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool
or other facility intended or used for the disposal of sewage;
   D.   The owner of any house, building or property used for human occupancy,
employment, recreation or other purposes, situated within the town, is hereby
required at his or her expense to install suitable toilet facilities therein,
and to connect such facilities directly with the proper public sewer in
accordance with the provisions of this code, within thirty (30) days after date
of official notice to connect.
      The following shall be exempted from the requirement of connecting to the
town's sewer system:
      1.   A residence, building or property used for human occupancy,
employment, recreation or other purposes where a public sewer is not located
within two hundred (200) feet of the property line as measured along a street,
alley, or right-of-way.
      Any person, firm or corporation affected by any notice, order,
determination or interpretation of the utility provisions of the Code of
Ordinances may request and shall be granted a hearing on the matter before the
Locust Grove Public Works Authority Board of Trustees, provided that such
person shall file in the office of the Town Clerk a written petition requesting
such hearing and setting forth a brief statement of the grounds for such
appeal. Such petition shall be filed within ten (10) days after the day the
notice, order, determination or interpretation is issued or rendered. Upon
receipt of such a petition, the matter shall be placed upon the agenda for a
hearing at the next regularly scheduled meeting of Locust Grove Public Works
Authority Board of Trustees. The petitioner shall be given written notice
thereof. At such hearing, the town official shall present any matter or
evidence relating to the appeal pending, and thereafter the petitioner shall be
given an opportunity to be heard and to show cause which such notice, order,
determination or interpretation should be modified or withdrawn. The town
official, petitioner, or any other interested party may appear in person or by
authorized representative.
   E.   In a building in which the building drain is too low to permit gravity
flow to the public sanitary sewer, the sanitary sewage shall be lifted by an
approved means and discharged to the building sewer or public sanitary sewer at
no expense to the town.
   F.   No person shall make connection of roof downspouts, exterior foundation
drains, areaway drains or other sources of surface runoff or groundwater to a
building sanitary sewer or building drain which in turn is connected directly
or indirectly to the public sanitary sewer, and all such connections existing
at the date of passage of this code shall be removed immediately.
   G.   The connection of the building sewer into a public sanitary sewer shall
conform to the requirements of the town plumbing codes or other applicable
rules and regulations of the town. All such connections shall be made gas tight
and water tight. Any deviation from the prescribed procedures and material must
be approved by the town inspector before installation.
   H.   The owner of any building or buildings which are connected to the
public sanitary sewer shall be required to operate and properly maintain the
building drains and building sanitary sewer in accordance with all provisions
of these regulations at no expense to the town. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-8: PRIVATE SEWAGE DISPOSAL:
Where a public sanitary sewer is not available under the provisions of the code
(greater than two hundred (200) ft.), the building sewer shall be connected to
a private sewage disposal system complying with the following provisions:
   A.   Before commencement of construction of a private sewage disposal
system, the owner shall first obtain a written permit from the town and ODEQ
which the applicant shall supplement by any plans, specifications, test
results, and other information as are deemed necessary by those departments;
   B.   A permit for a private sewage disposal system shall not become
effective until the installation is completed to the satisfaction of the town
and ODEQ. They shall be allowed to inspect the work at any stage of
construction and, in any event, the applicant for the permit shall notify the
inspector when the work is ready for final inspection, and before any
underground portions are covered;
   C.   The type, capacities, location, and layout of a private sewage disposal
system shall comply with all recommendations of the town and ODEQ;
   D.   The owner shall operate and maintain the private sewage disposal
facilities in a proper and sanitary manner at all times, at no expense to the
town;
   E.   At such time as a public sanitary sewer becomes available to a property
served by a private sewage disposal system, a direct connection shall be made
by the owner to the public sewer in compliance with these regulations and any
septic tanks, cesspools, and similar private sewage disposal facilities shall
be abandoned and filled with suitable material to the satisfaction of the town;
and
   F.   Private sewage disposal systems shall comply with any additional
requirements that may be imposed by the town-county health officer or other
authority having jurisdiction thereof. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-9: PERMITS REQUIRED:
No person, as defined in this chapter, shall uncover, make any connections with
or opening into, use, alter, or disturb any public or private sanitary sewer or
appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the town
pursuant to the following provisions:
   A.   For a building sewer permit the owner or his or her agent shall make
application on a form furnished by the town. The permit application shall be
supplemented by any plans, specifications, or other information considered
pertinent in the judgment of the town. When the application is complete, and
all fees associated with the permit have been paid, the town may issue the
permit;
   B.   Each application for building sewer shall be signed by the licensed
master plumber responsible for the work to be performed or the town inspector
as shown on the application. The work done under the permit shall be supervised
by the licensed master plumber and the town inspector;
   C.   A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every
individually owned residential or commercial building and each such building
shall have its own connection to the public sewer. Multiple ownership of
building sewers is prohibited and private ownership of sewers to which the
public connects is prohibited and declared a public offense;
   D.   The size, slope, alignment, and materials of construction of a building
sanitary sewer; and the methods to be used in excavation, placing of the pipe,
joining, testing and backfilling the trench, shall all conform to the rules and
regulations of the Oklahoma Department of Environmental Quality (ODEQ) and the
International Building Code, the latest edition thereof, as published by the
International Code Council (ICC) with modifications by the Oklahoma Unified
Building Code Commission (OUBCC);
   E.   The applicant for the building sewer connection permit shall notify the
plumbing inspector when the building sewer is ready for inspection and
connection to the public sanitary sewer. The connection shall be made under the
supervision of the plumbing inspector. No work shall be covered until the
inspection and tests have been made and written approval given;
   F.   Test tees and plugs shall be installed, where the building sewer
connects to the wye or stub from the public sanitary sewer, in order that a
hydrostatic test may be performed by the plumber in the presence of the
plumbing inspector. In the event connection is made to a manhole, no test tee
need be installed;
   G.   Building sewers shall be connected to a public sanitary sewer not
smaller than six inches (6") and no larger than twenty-four (24) inches, and
only through wye-shaped connections;
   H.   In the event the building sewer is connected to a manhole, it shall be
inserted through the wall not more than two feet (2') above the bottom or a
satisfactory drop shall be installed. The connection shall be thoroughly
patched inside and out with appropriate cement mortar to make a water tight
connection; and
   I.   All excavations for building sewer installation shall be adequately
guarded with barricades so as to completely protect the public from all
hazards. Streets, sidewalks, parkways, and all other property disturbed in the
course of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the Town Clerk
or their designee. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-10: PERMITS FOR DISCONNECTING SEWERS:
   A.   Before any dwelling or other building having a connection to the sewer
system is moved or demolished, the building sanitary sewer shall be
disconnected at the adjacent property line.
   B.   The remaining portion of the building sanitary sewer leading into the
public sanitary sewer shall be sealed and made water tight.
   C.   Prior to the disconnection of any such building sanitary sewer, a
permit shall be obtained from the inspections section of the town.
      1.   After the disconnection seal is made and before the work is covered,
the plumbing inspector shall be notified.
      2.   No work shall be covered until the inspection has been made and the
work approved. Written notices of approval shall be given. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-
2021)
9-3-11: PROHIBITED DISCHARGE STANDARDS:
   A.   No user shall introduce or cause to be introduced into the POTW,
directly or indirectly, any pollutant or wastewater which causes pass through
or interference. These general prohibitions apply to all industrial users of
the POTW whether or not they are subject to categorical pretreatment standards
or any other national, state or local pretreatment standards or requirement. In
addition, the following pollutants shall not be introduced into the POTW:
      1.   Pollutants which create a fire or explosive hazard in the municipal
wastewater collection and POTW, including, but not limited to, waste streams
with a closed-cup flashpoint of less than one hundred forty (140) degrees
Fahrenheit, sixty (60) degrees centigrade using the test methods specified in
40 CFR 261.21. At no time, shall two (2) successive readings on an explosion
hazard meter, at the point of discharge into the POTW, or at any point in the
POTW, be more than five percent (5%) nor any single reading over ten percent
(10%) of the lower explosive limit (LEL) of the meter;
      2.   Solid or viscous substances in amounts which will cause obstruction
of the flow in the POTW resulting in interference, but in no case solids
greater than one-half inch;
      3.   Any wastewater having a pH less than five and five tenths (5 5/10)
or more than twelve (12) S.U., or otherwise causing corrosive structural damage
to the POTW or equipment, or endangering town personnel;
      4.   Any wastewater containing pollutants including oxygen-demanding
pollutants (BOD, etc.), released in a discharge at a flow rate or pollutant
concentration which, either singly or by interaction with other pollutants,
will cause interference with either the POTW; or any wastewater treatment or
sludge process, or which will constitute a hazard to humans or animals;
      5.   Any noxious or malodorous liquids, gases, solids or other wastewater
which either singly or by interaction with other wastes are sufficient to
create a public nuisance or hazard to life or to prevent entry into the sewer
for maintenance and repair;
      6.   Any substance which may cause the POTW effluent or any other product
of the POTW such as residues, sludge, or scums, to be unsuitable for
reclamation and reuse or to interfere with the reclamation process. In no case,
shall a substance discharged to the POTW cause the POTW to be in noncompliance
with sludge use or disposal criteria, guidelines, or regulations developed
under Section 405 of the Act; any criteria, guidelines, or regulations
affecting sludge use or disposal developed pursuant to the Solid Waste Disposal
Act, the Clean Air Act, the Toxic Substances Control Act, or state criteria
applicable to the sludge management method being used;
      7.   Any wastewater which imparts color which cannot be removed in the
treatment process, which consequently imparts color to the treatment plant's
effluent thereby violating the POTW NPDES permit or interferes with the
operation of the POTW such as, but not limited to, dye wastes and vegetable
tanning solutions;
      8.   Any wastewater having a temperature higher than sixty-five (65)
degrees centigrade, one hundred fifty (150) degrees Fahrenheit, or capable of
inhibiting biological activity in the POTW resulting in interference, but in no
case wastewater with a temperature at the introduction into the POTW which
exceeds forty (40) degrees centigrade, one hundred four (104) degrees
Fahrenheit;
      9.   Any wastewater containing any radioactive wastes or isotopes except
as specifically approved by the industrial pretreatment coordinator in
compliance with state or federal regulations;
      10.   Any free or emulsified fats, waxes., greases or oils of animal or
vegetable origin in excess of two hundred (200) mg/L which may solidify or
become viscous at temperatures between thirty-two (32) degrees Fahrenheit (zero
degrees centigrade) and one hundred fifty (150) degrees Fahrenheit sixty-five
(65) degrees centigrade and which, in the opinion of the control authority, it
appears probable that such wastes:
         a.   Can deposit grease or oil in the sewer system in such a manner as
to obstruct the sewer;
         b.   Can overload the discharger's skimming and grease handling
equipment;
         c.   Are not amendable to bacterial action and will therefor pass to
the receiving stream without being affected by normal sewage treatment process;
or
         d.   Can have deleterious effects on the treatment process due to
excessive quantities or concentrations.
      11.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage grinder equipped with a motor of three-quarters
horsepower (hp) or greater shall be subject to the review and approval of the
plumbing inspector;
      12.   Petroleum oil, non-biodegradable cutting oil, or products of
mineral oil origin, in amounts that will cause interference;
      13.   Any pollutants which result in the presence of toxic gases, vapors
or fumes within the POTW in a quantity that may cause actual worker health and
safety problems;
      14.   Any trucked or hauled pollutants, except at discharge points
designated by the town;
      15.   Stormwater, surface water, ground water, artesian well water, roof
runoff, subsurface drainage, swimming pool drainage, condensate, deionized
water, noncontact cooling water, and unpolluted industrial wastewater, unless
specifically authorized by the industrial pretreatment coordinator;
      16.   Any sludge, screenings, or other residues from the pretreatment of
industrial wastes;
      17.   Any medical wastes, except as specifically authorized by the
industrial pretreatment coordinator in a wastewater discharge permit;
      18.   Any wastewater causing the treatment plant's effluent to fail a
toxicity test;
      19.   Any wastes containing detergents, surface active agents, or other
substances which may cause excessive foaming in the POTW; or
      20.   Any discharge or discharge creating a condition for the POTW or the
receiving waters, which violates any statute, rule, regulation or ordinance of
any public agency, including EPA and ODEQ.
   B.   Wastes prohibited by this section shall not be processed or stored in
such manner that they could be discharged to the POTW.
   C.   All floor drains located in process or materials storage areas must
discharge to the industrial user's pretreatment facility before connecting with
the POTW.
   D.   Except as to categories in subsections 1, 2, 3, 4, 10, 12, 13 and 14 of
subsection A of this section, the remaining categories outlined in subsection A
of this section, shall be prohibited. When the industrial pretreatment
coordinator determines that a user is contributing to the POTW, any of the
enumerated substances in such amounts as to interfere with the operation of the
POTW, the superintendent industrial pretreatment coordinator shall take
appropriate enforcement action in accordance with the enforcement response plan
hereby incorporated herein by reference thereto. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-12: INTERCEPTORS FOR GREASE:
Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the opinion of the
superintendent pretreatment coordinator, they are necessary for the proper
handling of wastewater containing excessive amounts of grease and oil, or sand;
except that such interceptors shall not be required for residential users. All
interception units shall be of type and capacity approved by the industrial
pretreatment coordinator and shall be so located to be easily accessible for
cleaning and inspection. Such interceptors shall be inspected, cleaned, and
repaired regularly, as needed, by the owner at his or her expense. (Ord. 2021-
01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-13: TAMPERING WITH SEWER SYSTEM PROHIBITED; PENALTY:
No person, as defined in this chapter, shall maliciously, willfully, or
knowingly break, alter, damage, destroy, uncover, deface, or tamper with any
structure, appurtenance, or equipment which is a part of the sewage works POTW.
Any person violating this provision shall be subject to a fine for each offense
and which shall not release any civil liability for damages and costs incident
to replacement of the facilities. All persons charged with violation of this
provision shall be entitled to trial by jury if required by Oklahoma Statutes.
(Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-14: COMPLIANCE MONITORING:
   A.   Inspection and sampling requirements are as follows:
      1.   The town will conduct at least one inspection and sampling visit
annually for each significant industrial user;
      2.   The town shall have the right to enter the facilities of any
industrial user to ascertain whether the purpose of this chapter, and any
permit or order issued hereunder, is being met and whether the industrial user
is complying with all requirements thereof. Industrial users shall allow the
industrial pretreatment coordinator or his or her representatives' ready access
to all parts of the premises for the purposes of inspection, sampling, records
examination and copying, and the performance of any additional duties:
         a.   Where an industrial user has security measures in force which
require proper identification and clearance before entry into its premises, the
industrial user shall make necessary arrangements with its security guards so
that, upon presentation of suitable identification, personnel from the town,
state, and EPA will be permitted to enter without delay, for the purposes of
performing their [text missing]. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-15: GENERAL PROVISIONS:
The inspector shall inspect and approve all drainage and sewer work installed
or to be installed in the town. He or she shall pass judgment upon all
connections to private or public property, up to and including the place where
such sewer work connects with the soil pipe. He or she shall approve such
connections when the same shall conform to the provisions of this chapter, and
no such connections shall be allowed without such approval. It is his or her
duty to cause all excavations to be properly filled and restored to safe
condition of usage. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-16: INGRESS:
Any other duly authorized employee of the town shall have the right of ingress
and egress to any private or public property for the discharge of their duties
hereunder. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-17: INSPECTION REQUIRED:
All drainage of buildings and all sewer work inside of private property lines
in the town must be done or installed in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter and all other applicable laws; and must be inspected by the plumbing
inspector, pursuant to §§ 9-3-7G, 9-3-8B and 9-3-9B, E, and F hereinafter, and
a certificate of inspection issued therefor before the same may be used or
connected with any public sewer, and all sewers and connections in streets or
alleys of the town must be inspected by the plumbing inspector. (Ord. 2021-01,
1-11-2021)
9-3-18: INSPECTION FEES:
The inspector shall charge a fee as set by the town council on all inspections
of each sewer job. An additional fee shall be charged for each extra trip of
the inspector caused by faulty work or work not being completed or ready for
inspection when the plumbing inspector is notified to make such inspection.
(Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-19: CERTIFICATE OF INSPECTION:
Any person, firm or corporation, as defined in this chapter, making sewer
connections must report the connections to the plumbing inspector as soon as
the job is ready for inspection, and must keep the connections open for
inspection until the inspection and compliance with this and other titles and
the statutes of the state applicable thereto are complete, then a certificate
of inspection shall thereupon be issued upon the payment of the fees therefor.
(Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-20: EXCAVATIONS IN STREET OR PUBLIC PROPERTY:
No person, as defined in this chapter, shall excavate or cause any excavation
in any street, alley, or other public place, or cut or cause to be cut any
curb, sidewalk or pavement in the town, in doing or for the purpose of doing
any work covered by this chapter, or any other work, without having a permit to
do so from the permitting department and without having deposited such sum of
money and having entered into such other undertaking as required by this or
other chapters of the code of the town, as a guarantee for the replacement and
reconstruction of such sidewalk, curb or pavement, approved by the town and
shall be located as to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and
inspection. The owner shall be responsible for operation and maintenance of
private grease, oil and sand traps. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-21: DAMAGES TO PUBLIC PROPERTY MUST BE REPAIRED:
All damages to sidewalks, curbs, sewers, paving or other property of the town
must be properly repaired or replaced by the person, firm or corporation
causing the damage, either by themselves or their agents, servants or
employees. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-22: EXCAVATIONS MUST BE REPAIRED:
Any person, as defined in the chapter, making, or causing to be made, any
excavation in any street, alley or other public place in the town, must cause
such excavation to be promptly and carefully refilled and repaired in
accordance with this or other chapters of the code of the town, and the failure
to do so shall constitute an offense under the provisions hereof. (Ord. 2021-
01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-23: INSPECTION WITHIN FORTY-EIGHT (48) HOURS:
It is the duty of the plumbing inspector in all cases when notified, to cause
inspection of all sewers in connection with sewage drainage within forty-eight
(48) hours after receipt of notice from the sewer contractor or person doing
the work in question that such work is ready for inspection. Holidays and
Sundays shall not be included in computing the forty-eight (48) hour period.
(Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-24: UNLAWFUL TO PROCEED WITHOUT PERMIT:
It is unlawful for any person, as defined in this chapter, to proceed with any
work connected or to be connected with any sewer system of the town, until a
permit for such work has been obtained from the inspections department;
provided that no permit shall be required for the making of minor repairs,
unless a portion or a section of the drain line or sewer line is out, removed,
or replaced. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-25: ALL PLUMBING MUST BE ACCESSIBLE FOR INSPECTION:
In all buildings or structures hereafter erected in the town, both public and
private, and in all buildings already erected wherein any plumbing is hereafter
installed, or wherein any sewer connection pipes shall be repaired or changed
on the sewer side of the tap, the drain, soil, waste, or any other pipe or
pipes, and all traps, shall be placed in the building and exposed to view for
ready inspection and test, and shall remain so exposed until approved by the
plumbing inspector. In no case shall a trap be inaccessible at any time. (Ord.
2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-26: CONNECTION OUTSIDE BUILDING:
The connection of a sewer pipe to the sanitary sewer main shall be made with a
proper tapping saddle, of the quality acceptable identified in current Building
Code Standards. However, this connection shall not be made until the work
inside and outside of the building has been tested, inspected and approved by
the plumbing inspector. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-27: DRAINS CONNECTED WITH SEWER:
It is the duty of each person, as defined in this chapter, connecting or
causing to be connected any drain, pipe or passage with any such sewer from any
building, structure or premises, to cause such drain, pipe or passage and
connection to be at all times adequate for its purpose and of such size and
dimension as to convey and allow freely to pass whatever may properly enter the
same. Whenever the lowest sewer inlet in a building or structure is less than
four feet (4') above the top of the sewer main at the point of connection or
junction with the main, then in such event it is the duty of each person, as
defined in this chapter, connecting or causing to be connected any sewer pipe
to a sewer main to place in the sewer pipe a check valve, to prevent sewer
back-ups in the event the sewer main or sewer pipe connected to the sewer main
becomes clogged. The sewer pipe must conform to the requirements set forth in
the International Building Codes latest edition as published by the
International Code Council (ICC) with modifications by the Oklahoma Unified
Building Code Commission (OUBCC), and be free from defects and cracks and so
molded that bells will receive the ends of the pipe freely. The same shall be
laid to outlet with an even grade, with a fall of at least one-quarter inch per
foot. In laying drain pipe, space must be excavated so that the bell end will
have a solid bearing with the entire pipe. Backfilling must be packed up to the
top of the pipe. Joints must be properly made and the inside of the joints must
be made smooth. Changes of directions must be made with regulation curves, and
all connections made with wide junctions. Ends not in immediate use must be
tightly stopped to prevent dirt from entering the pipe. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-
2021)
9-3-28: FIBER PIPE NOT ALLOWED:
No fiber type pipe or fittings shall be used or permitted to be used for
connection to the town sewage disposal system. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-29: PROHIBITED SEWER CONNECTIONS:
No roof or surface water drain pipe shall be connected so as to discharge into
a sanitary sewer. No dam or other construction shall be placed in any sewer,
unless permission to do so is expressly granted in writing by the town. In case
any material discharged from any premises into any public or private sewer
cannot, in the opinion of the town be rendered harmless to the public sewer and
to the public health, such material shall be ordered excluded from any public,
private, or district sewer. The town shall, in writing, notify the person or
persons owning or occupying such premises to exclude such material from the
sewer, and a failure to comply with such notice shall constitute a violation of
this chapter. If catch basins are needed to accomplish such exclusions, the
written notice shall direct the building of such catch basins, within thirty
(30) days after serving of such notice. If after the expiration of the thirty
(30) days the order shall not be complied with, the person, firm or corporation
owning or controlling the premises shall be deemed guilty of a violation of
this chapter. Where no sanitary sewers are accessible, sinks shall waste
through a grease trap and not less than thirty feet (30') of filled tile
disposal. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-30: DRAINAGE OBSTRUCTIONS:
If the drainage discharged from any home, business, or establishment shall
produce or form a deposit obstructing a sewer, the plumbing inspector shall
immediately cause the removal of the obstruction, keeping account of the cost
of such removal, and shall certify an account of the cost to the person or
persons causing the obstruction; and if such person or persons shall fail,
refuse or neglect to pay the sum to the town within five (5) days after demand
has been made, they shall be guilty of a public offense. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-
2021)
9-3-31: SEPARATE DRAINAGE FOR EVERY BUILDING:
Every building shall be separately and independently connected with a public
sewer, where there is any such sewer adjacent to such building. The entire
plumbing and drainage system of each building shall be entirely separate and
independent from that of every other building, except that where there is more
than one building on the lot, the sewer of the first building may be extended
to serve the adjoining building on permission granted by the town which
permission shall be in writing. A lot shall be any plot of ground, regardless
of size, containing one dwelling and one garage or out-building. Each and every
house occupied or to be occupied as a residence, must have a separate drain to
the connection with the sewer. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-32: SEWER INSTALLATION TO BE UNDERGROUND:
All sewers shall be put in the ground at a sufficient depth to be safe from
breaking by the ordinary use to which such property may be subjected. All sewer
pipe must be placed at least eighteen inches (18") below the top of the ground
measured from the top of such pipe, except when such depth is impossible or
impracticable for lack of fall, in which case iron pipe caulked with lead shall
be used between the building and the point where the depth above-mentioned may
be acquired. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-33: APPORTIONMENT OF COST FOR CONNECTION OF PROPERTY OUTSIDE SEWER
DISTRICT:
When public sewers have been constructed, and the cost thereof has been wholly
or partly paid out of the funds of the town, and the owner of any abutting
property makes application for a permit to tap such sewer, no permit shall be
issued to such abutting owner unless he or she shall have first paid to the
town the assessment or assessments levied against the property for the cost of
the sewer, or in the case where his or her property has not been assessed or
where any intended assessment has been held invalid or considered invalid by
the town, unless he or she pays a sum proportionate to that paid by other
similar property owners who have been assessed. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-34: PROPERTY OUTSIDE SEWER DISTRICT; HOW CONNECTED:
Any person, as defined in this chapter, owning property or in charge of
property not included in any sewer district which has been established,
desiring to connect with the sewer owned and operated by the town nearest the
property owned by such person, as defined in this chapter, shall first file
with the town a written application therefor, signed by the person, as defined
in this chapter, giving the legal description of the property and waiving any
right to protest any assessment levied against the property for the subsequent
installation of such sewer, providing the assessment is of the same proportion
as assessments upon other property affected by the installation of the sewer.
The plumbing inspector, upon receiving the application, shall make an
inspection of the property specified in the application and if found
practicable and that the connection will not be likely to overload the sewer if
connected thereto, shall grant the permit. The fee for the permit shall be as
set by the town council, the fee to be collected prior to the time any permit
is issued. (Ord. 2021-01, 1-11-2021)
9-3-35: PENALTY PROVISIONS:
Any person, as defined in this chapter, found to be violating any provisions of
this chapter, except §
9-3-7D, shall be served written notice stating the nature of the violation and
providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory correction thereof. The
offender shall, within the period of time stated in such notice, permanently
cease all violations:
   A.   The owner of any building drains and building sanitary sewers and any
private disposal system shall keep such facilities clean and in good repair.
Failure to comply with written notice by the town to make repairs or remove
violations including those existing at the time of passage of this chapter,
shall subject the violator to fine and punishment as provided in this code.
Each day of continued violation shall constitute a separate chargeable offense;
and
   B.   Any person, as defined in this chapter, found guilty of violating any
of the provisions of this chapter, or refusing to connect with the public
sanitary sewer within the time prescribed by proper order, on conviction
thereof, shall be punished by fine which shall not release any civil liability.
Each day of continued violation shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord.
2021-01, 1-11-2021)
TITLE 10
BUILDING AND DEVELOPMENT
CHAPTER 1
PENALTY PROVISIONS
SECTION:
10-1-1: Violation; Penalty
10-1-2: Relief In Courts
10-1-1: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who engages in any business, trade or vocation for which a license,
permit, certificate or registration is required by this title, without first
having a valid license, permit, certificate or registration as required, or who
shall fail to do anything required by this title or by any Code adopted in this
title, or who shall otherwise violate any provision of this title, or of any
Code adopted in this title, or who shall violate any lawful regulation or order
made by any of the officers provided in this title shall be guilty of an
offense, punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. Each day upon which a violation continues shall be deemed a
separate offense. (2014 Code § 5-801)
10-1-2: RELIEF IN COURTS:
No penalty imposed by and pursuant to this title shall interfere with the right
of the Town also to apply to the proper courts of the State for mandamus, an
injunction, or other appropriate action against such person. (2014 Code § 5-
802)
CHAPTER 2
BUILDING CODE AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
10-2-1: Building Code
10-2-2: Permit Requirements
10-2-3: Violation; Penalty
10-2-4: Tiny Houses
10-2-1: BUILDING CODE:
   A.   Adoption Of Code: A certain document, at least one copy of which is on
file in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer, being marked and designated as
the International Building Code, the latest edition thereof, as published by
the International Code Council (ICC) with modifications by the Oklahoma Unified
Building Code Commission (OUBCC) is hereby adopted as the Building Code of the
Town for the control of buildings and structures as therein provided. Each and
all of the regulations, provisions, penalties, conditions and terms of the
Building Code are hereby referred to, adopted, incorporated and made a part
hereof as if fully set out in this subsection, with the additions, insertions,
deletions and changes, if any, prescribed in subsection B of this section.
(2018 Code)
   B.   Amendments To Code: The following sections of the Town's Building Code
are hereby revised:
Insert: Offenses are punishable by fine and imprisonment as provided in section
1-4-1 of the Town Code.
At all other applicable places, insert: Town of Locust Grove, Board of Trustees
and Town Code as necessary.
(2014 Code § 5-102; amd. 2018 Code)
10-2-2: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permit Required:
      1.   No building or other structure shall be built, enlarged, altered or
moved as required in the Building Code, nor any mobile home located, relocated
or constructed, without a building permit issued by the Town Code Enforcement
Officer.
      2.   Whenever a building or structure is to be moved from without the
Town to a location within the Town or from one location within the Town to
another location within the Town, a building permit is required.
      3.   A building permit shall be issued for building or construction of
any type including fences, driveways, installation of storm shelters, sheds, or
garages, among other construction or building types.
   B.   Application For Permit: A person desiring a building permit shall
submit an application to the Town Code Enforcement Officer. The applicant shall
submit with the application such reasonable information as the Code Enforcement
Officer may require to enable the officer to determine whether granting the
permit would be in accordance with the requirements of the ordinances of the
Town.
   C.   Issuance Of Permit; Fee And Exemptions:
      1.   If the applicant is in accordance with the requirements of the
ordinances and laws, the Code Enforcement Officer shall issue the permit upon
the payment by the applicant of a building permit fee which may be set by
motion or resolution of the Town Board of Trustees. A current copy of the fee
schedule shall be kept in the Office of the Town Code Enforcement Officer.
      2.   All buildings being constructed by public bodies, such as the State,
counties, school districts, municipalities, and tax exempt organizations, shall
be exempt from the payment of fees for building permits. Such bodies shall
comply with all other regulations governing the construction of any building in
the Town.
   D.   Scope Of Permit: A building permit covers the initial plumbing,
mechanical and electrical installations to be made in connection with the
building. (2014 Code § 5-106; amd. 2018 Code)
10-2-3: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
A violation of this chapter shall be deemed a misdemeanor and shall be
punishable by fine. Any person, firm or corporation who violates or refuses to
comply with any of the provisions of this chapter shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2014 Code § 5-103)
10-2-4: TINY HOUSES:
   A.   Title: This section is hereby referenced as the Locust Grove Tiny House
Ordinance.
   B.   Definitions: The following words and terms shall for the purpose of
this section have the meanings shown herein.
DWELLING: A dwelling is any building that contains one (1) dwelling unit
intended to be used and occupied as a residence.
DWELLING UNIT: A single unit that provides complete independent living
facilities such as living, sleeping, eating, cooking and sanitation.
EGRESS ROOF ACCESS WINDOW: A skylight or roof window designed and installed to
satisfy the emergency escape and rescue opening requirement of paragraph E8
herein.
HABITABLE SPACE: Any space within a building that is used for living, sleeping,
eating or cooking. Spaces such as bathrooms, toilet rooms, closets, halls, and
storage spaces are not considered as habitable spaces.
LANDING PLATFORM: A landing provided as the top step of a stairway accessing a
loft.
LOFT: Within a tiny house is defined as a floor level that is located more than
thirty inches (30") above the main floor, open to the main floor on at least
one side with a ceiling height less than six feet eight inches (6' 8") and used
as a living or sleeping space.
PERMIT: Written permit issued by the Town Clerk permitting the placement,
alteration or extension of tiny homes under the provisions of this section and
regulations thereof.
PERSON: Any natural individual, firm, trust, partnership, association,
corporation.
TINY HOUSE: A dwelling to be used as permanent housing that is six hundred
forty to seven hundred fifty (640 - 750) square feet of total living space,
excluding lofts, porches, garages and other space not heated or cooled by any
means, with two hundred (200) sq. ft. of exterior or open space per house.
   C.   Permits/Applications:
      1.   Application Requirements For A Permit:
         a.   All tiny house builders must complete an application for building
a tiny house including, but not limited to, the following:
            1)   Name, address, telephone number of applicant.
            2)   Location, legal property description, block and lot where tiny
house is to be located.
            3)   Dimensions of the tiny house.
            4)   Description of material being used to build the tiny house.
Premanufactured tiny houses are not allowed within town corporate limits.
            5)   Plat or blueprints identifying connections to town services
including water, sewer and sanitation.
            6)   Photographs of the tiny house, if available.
         b.   Issuance Of Permit: In considering the application for building a
tiny house, the Town Board of Trustees or designated building inspector may
take into account the proposed location of the tiny house in relation to the
present and anticipated land use and development. After review of the
application by the Board of Trustees and determining the application and the
proposed home complies with this Ordinance and other applicable laws, codes,
regulations and ordinances, the permit shall be issued.
         c.   Denial Of Application/Hearing: Any person whose application for a
permit has been denied may, within ten (10) days of the denial, request in
writing to the Town Clerk a re-hearing by the Board of Trustees on the matter
including additional evidence at the hearing if desired.
   D.   Basic Tiny House Requirements:
      1.   The tiny house must have a driveway.
      2.   The tiny house must be located on a common access route/internal
street and have an assigned address.
      3.   The tiny house must be connected to town utilities, which is water
and sewer services. Sewer service is essential to dispose of all human waste.
No composting toilets will be permitted.
      4.   Tiny house must pass the inspection of the Town Board of Trustees,
or the building inspector, or any subsequent structural standards which may be
adopted by the town.
      5.   More than one (1) tiny house can be located on a lot.
      6.   It shall be unlawful to locate a tiny home on wheels, classified as
a recreational vehicle (RV), as a permanent dwelling within the corporate
limits of Locust Grove.
   E.   Tiny House Regulations:
      1.   The tiny house must be on a permanent foundation with at least six
(6) inches of cement footing, which is steel reinforced for load bearing walls.
      2.   Tiny house ceilings:
         a.   The minimum ceiling height for the three (3) main areas within a
tiny house:
            1)   Habitable spaces and hallways shall not have a ceiling height
less than six feet eight inches (6' 8").
            2)   Bathrooms, toilet rooms, and kitchens shall not have a ceiling
height less than six feet four inches (6' 4"). Obstructions including, but not
limited to beams, girders, ducts and lighting, shall not extend below these
minimum ceiling heights.
            3)   Lofts are permitted to be less than six feet eight inches (6'
8"). Portions of the loft with sloped ceilings that measure less than three
feet (3') from the finished floor to the finished ceiling do not contribute to
the minimum required area for a loft.
      3.   Tiny House Lofts:
         a.   A loft used as a sleeping or living space shall meet the minimum
area and dimension requirements of thirty-five (35) sq. ft. in floor area and
not less than five feet (5') in any horizontal dimension.
         b.   Portions of a loft with a sloped ceiling measuring less than
three feet (3') from the finished floor to the finished ceiling shall not be
considered as contributing to the minimum required area for the loft.
            1)   Exception: Under gable roofs with a minimum slope of six (6)
units vertical and twelve (12) units horizontal (fifty percent (50%) slope),
portions of a loft with a sloped ceiling measuring less than sixteen inches
(16") from the finished floor to the finished ceiling shall be considered as
contributing to the minimum required area for the loft.
         c.   Loft Guards:
            1)   Loft guards shall be located along the open side of lofts.
Loft guards shall be not less than thirty-six inches (36") in height or one-
half (½) of the clear height to the ceiling, whichever is less.
      4.   Stairways:
         a.   Stairways accessing lofts shall not be less than seventeen inches
(17") in clear width at or above the handrail. The width of the handrail shall
be not less than twenty inches (20").
         b.   The headroom in stairways accessing a loft shall be not less than
six feet two inches (6' 2") as measured vertically, from a sloped line
connecting the tread or landing platform nosings in the middle of their width.
         c.   Handrails and stairway guards must comply with the same code
sections used for a traditional home.
      5.   Treads And Risers:
         a.   Risers for stairs accessing a loft shall be not less than seven
inches (7") and not more than twelve inches (12") in height. Tread depth and
riser height shall be calculated in accordance with one the following formulas:
            1)   Tread depth shall be twenty inches (20") minus four-thirds (4/
3) of the riser height.
            2)   Riser height shall be fifteen inches (15") minus one-half (½)
of the tread depth.
      6.   Landing Platforms:
         a.   The top tread and riser of stairways accessing lofts shall be
constructed as a landing platform where the loft ceiling height is less than
six feet two inches (6' 2") where the stairway meets the loft.
         b.   The landing platform shall be eighteen inches (18") to twenty-two
inches (22") in depth measured from the nosing of the landing platform to the
edge of the loft, and sixteen inches (16") to eighteen inches (18") height
measured from the landing platform to the loft floor.
      7.   Ladders:
         a.   Ladders accessing lofts shall have a rung width of not less than
twelve inches (12"), and ten inches (10") spacing between rungs. Ladders shall
be capable of supporting a two hundred (200) lb. load on any rung. Rung spacing
shall be uniform within three eights inches (”).
         b.   Ladders shall be installed at seventy (70) to eighty (80) degrees
from horizontal.
      8.   Emergency Escape And Rescue Openings:
         a.   Basements and every sleeping room shall have at least one
operable emergency and rescue opening. Such opening shall open directly into a
public street, public alley, yard or court. Where basements contain one or more
sleeping rooms, emergency egress and rescue openings shall be required in each
sleeping room, but shall not be required in adjoining areas of the basement.
         b.   Where emergency escape and rescue openings are provided they
shall have a sill height of not more than forty-four inches (44") above the
floor. Where a door opening having a threshold below the adjacent ground
elevation serves as an emergency escape and rescue opening and is provided with
a bulkhead enclosure, the bulkhead enclosure shall comply with paragraph
E.8.c.7) below herein. The net clear opening dimensions required by this
section shall be obtained by the normal operation of the emergency escape and
rescue opening from the inside. Emergency escape and rescue openings with a
finished sill height below the adjacent ground elevation shall be provided with
a window well in according with paragraph E.8.c.5) below.
         c.   Exception: Basements used only to house mechanical equipment and
not exceeding total floor area of two hundred (200) sq. ft.
            1)   Minimum Opening Area: All emergency escape and rescue openings
shall have a minimum net clear opening of 5.7 sq. ft.
               a)   Exception: Grade floor openings shall have a minimum net
clear opening of five (5) sq. ft.
            2)   Minimum Opening Height: The minimum net clear opening height
shall be twenty four inches (24").
            3)   Minimum Opening Width: The minimum net clear opening width
shall be twenty inches (20").
            4)   Operational Constraints: Emergency escape and rescue openings
shall be operational from the inside of the room without the use of keys, tools
or special knowledge.
            5)   Window Wells: Minimum horizontal area of the window well shall
be nine (9) sq. ft. with a minimum horizontal projection and width of thirty-
six inches (36"). The area of the window well shall allow the emergency escape
and rescue opening to be fully opened.
               a)   Exception: Ladder or steps required in paragraph E8.c.6)
herein shall be permitted to encroach a maximum of six inches (6") into the
required dimensions of the window well.
            6)   Ladder And Steps: Window wells with a vertical depth greater
than forty-four inches (44") shall be equipped with a permanently affixed
ladder or steps usable with the window in the fully open position. Ladders or
rungs shall have an inside width of at least twelve inches (12"), shall project
at least three inches (3") from the wall and shall be spaced not more than
eighteen inches (18") on center vertically for the full height of the window
well.
            7)   Bulkhead Enclosures: Bulkhead enclosures shall provide direct
access to the basement. The bulkhead enclosure with the door panels in the
fully open position shall provide the minimum net clear opening of 5.7 sq. ft.
            8)   Bars, Grilles, Covers And Screens: Bars, grilles, covers,
screens or similar devices are permitted to be placed over emergency escape and
rescue openings, bulkhead enclosures, or window wells that serve such openings,
provided the minimum net clear opening size of 5.7 ft., opening height of
twenty- four inches (24") and opening width of twenty inches (20") and such
devices shall be releasable or removable from the inside without the use of a
key, tool, special knowledge or force greater than that which is required for
normal operation of the escape and rescue opening.
            9)   Emergency Escape Windows Under Decks And Porches: Emergency
escape windows are allowed to be installed under decks and porches provided the
location of the deck allows the emergency escape window to be fully opened and
provides a path not less than thirty-six inches (36") in height to a yard or
court.
   F.   Penalty Provision: Any person violating of this section, or any portion
thereof, shall upon conviction be guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall be fined
not less than two hundred dollars ($200.00) for each day that such violation
continues. Each day may be considered a separate offense and punishable
accordingly.
   G.   Adoption Of Amendment:
Title 10, Chapter 2, of the Locust Grove Building Code is hereby amended to
establish development standards and regulations for tiny houses on a permanent
foundation that is one hundred fifty to seven hundred (150 - 700) square feet
of total living space, used as a permanent residence within the corporate
limits of the Town of Locust Grove, and providing for issuance of permits and
collection of fees for same. (Ord. 2022-03, 10-10-2022)
CHAPTER 3
PLUMBING CODE AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
10-3-1: Plumbing Code
10-3-2: Plumbing Contractors
10-3-3: Permits And Inspections
10-3-4: Violation; Penalty
10-3-1: PLUMBING CODE:
   A.   Adoption Of Code: A certain document, at least one copy of which is on
file in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer, being marked and designated as
the International Plumbing Code, the latest version thereof, and any revisions
or amendments thereto, as published by the International Code Council (ICC)
with modifications by the Oklahoma Unified Building Code Commission (OUBCC), is
hereby adopted as the Plumbing Code of the Town for the control of buildings
and structures as therein provided. Each and all of the regulations,
provisions, penalties, conditions and terms of the Plumbing Code are hereby
referred to, adopted and made a part hereof as if fully set out in this
subsection, with additions, insertions and changes, if any, prescribed in
subsection B of this section. (2014 Code § 5-201; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Amendments To Code: The following sections are hereby revised as
follows:
Insert: Applicable fees are as set by the Town by motion or resolution.
Insert: Offenses are punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of the Town Code.
(2014 Code § 5-202; amd. 2018 Code)
10-3-2: PLUMBING CONTRACTORS:
   A.   Definitions: The phrases and words "journeyman plumber", "plumber's
apprentice", "plumbing contractor", and "plumbing", when used in the
ordinances, regulations and other official acts and communications of the Town,
shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them by 59 Oklahoma Statutes
section 1001 et seq., the State Plumbing License Law, unless the context
clearly indicates a different meaning.
   B.   Registration Required: It is unlawful for any person to engage in the
business, trade, or occupation of a plumbing contractor (otherwise known as a
master plumber), or of a journeyman plumber, or of a plumber's apprentice in
the Town unless he is registered with the Town and has a current and valid
certificate of registration issued by the Town.
   C.   Qualifications For Certificate: Only persons who have current and valid
licenses as plumbing contractors or as journeyman plumbers issued by the State
Construction Industries Board, as provided by law, may register as such with
the Town. Only persons who have a current and valid certificate of registration
as plumber's apprentices issued by the state Construction Industries Board, as
provided by law, may register as such with the Town. Any license issued to a
firm is not transferable. If a person ceases to be associated with a licensed
firm, the firm is required to secure a new license in the name of the
qualified, licensed entity or person.
   D.   Application For Certificate: Applicants for certificates of
registration, after complying with the laws of the State and with this section,
and after payment of the fee set by the Town, shall be registered by the Town
Clerk-Treasurer.
   E.   Required Fees: The fees for registration shall be set by the Town Board
of Trustees by motion or resolution.
   F.   Expiration Of Registration; Renewals:
      1.   The registration shall expire annually, but may be renewed from year
to year. Plumbing contractors and journeymen plumbers desiring to renew their
registration shall furnish the same evidence of compliance with State licensing
laws and bond as set forth by the State.
      2.   All plumbing registrations not renewed within ninety (90) days after
the date of expiration thereof shall be canceled, and a new application for
registration must be made and the fee for new registration paid.
   G.   Revocation Of Registration: The Town Board of Trustees, upon at least
ten (10) days' notice and adequate opportunity for a public hearing, may revoke
the Town registration of any plumbing contractor or journeyman plumber for
violating any provisions of the ordinances or regulations of the Town relating
to the installation of plumbing or for any other cause specified in the State
Plumbing License Law. (2014 Code § 5-203; amd. 2018 Code)
10-3-3: PERMITS AND INSPECTIONS:
   A.   Permit Requirements:
      1.   Permit Required: No plumbing work shall be undertaken without a
permit from the Code Enforcement Officer.
      2.   Application For Permit: A person desiring a plumbing permit shall
submit an application to the Code Enforcement Officer. The applicant shall
submit with the application such reasonable information as the Code Enforcement
Officer may require to enable the applicant to determine whether granting the
permit would be in accordance with the requirements of the ordinances of the
Town.
      3.   Permit Fees: The schedule of permit fees may be set forth by
resolution or motion of the Town Board of Trustees. Such payment will be made
upon application.
   B.   Inspections: Inspection of such work must conform to the guidelines set
forth in this Code. (2014 Code § 5-204; amd. 2018 Code)
10-3-4: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
A violation of this chapter shall be deemed a misdemeanor and shall be
punishable by fine. Any person, firm or corporation who violates or refuses to
comply with any of the provisions of this chapter shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2014 Code § 5-205)
CHAPTER 4
ELECTRICAL CODE AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
10-4-1: Electrical Code Adopted
10-4-2: Electrical Contractors
10-4-3: Inspection Fee
10-4-4: Utility Connection Requirements
10-4-5: Violation; Penalty
10-4-1: ELECTRICAL CODE ADOPTED:
The National Electrical Code, the latest edition thereof, as approved by the
American Standards Association, for the installation of electrical wiring,
devices and equipment, is hereby adopted as the minimum standard for the
installation of all electrical wiring, devices and equipment in the Town,
except as otherwise specifically provided in this chapter. The National
Electrical Code is hereby made a part of this section as fully and to the same
extent as if copied herein in full; provided, that the present or current issue
of the National Electrical Code and any subsequent amendments thereto shall be
considered as the National Electrical Code as that term is used herein. A copy
of the Code is on file in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer for public use
and inspection. (2014 Code § 5-301; amd. 2018 Code)
10-4-2: ELECTRICAL CONTRACTORS:
   A.   Registration Requirements:
      1.   Town Registration And State License Required:
         a.   It is unlawful for any person to engage in the business, trade or
vocation of electrical contractor, journeyman electrician or apprentice
electrician without a certificate of registration, and any renewal, to be
secured from the Town.
         b.   No person may be registered with the Town as a contractor,
journeyman or apprentice unless he possesses a valid and current State license
issued by the State and pays the registration fee in such sum as set by the
Town Board of Trustees by motion or resolution.
      2.   Fees: The initial fee for a registration certificate, and any
renewal, to be paid to the Town Clerk-Treasurer, shall be as set by the Board
of Trustees.
      3.   Bond Requirements: Every person receiving a certificate as an
electrical contractor shall file with the Town Clerk- Treasurer a bond in such
sum as set by the Town Board of Trustees, executed with a surety company
authorized to do business in the State. The bond shall be conditioned that the
principal will install all electrical wiring, fixtures, appliances, and
equipment in accordance with the law and the ordinances and other regulations
of the Town relating to electrical installations and in a workmanlike manner;
that the principal shall, without further cost to the person for whom the work
was done, remedy any defective or faulty work caused by poor workmanship or
inferior or nonstandard material; and that the Town may be firmly indemnified
and held harmless from any and all costs, expenses or damage resulting from the
performance of his work as an electrical contractor or apprentice electrician,
as the case may be.
      4.   Nontransferability Of Certificate: The certificate is not
transferable to any other individual or company.
      5.   Renewals: A registration certificate must be renewed within ninety
(90) days following expiration of the certificate. After the expiration, an
application for a new certificate must be requested and the initial fee paid
again.
      6.   Exemptions: For the installing of bell, telephone or signal systems
not using over twelve (12) volts, no registration or bond will be required. The
installation of same must comply with all other requirements of the ordinances
of the Town.
      7.   Revocation Of Certificate: After adequate opportunity for a hearing,
the Town Board may revoke the certificate of an electrical contractor, an
apprentice electrician, or a journeyman electrician. (2014 Code § 5-302)
   B.   Defective Workmanship And Materials:
      1.   Any person, firm or corporation engaged in the business of
electrical contracting for the installation of wiring and apparatus for
electric light, heat or power in the Town who fails to correct promptly any
defects in any work done by him contrary to this Code, after having been
notified by the electrical inspector, shall not be issued any further permits
until such defects have been corrected; and in any case in which any person
shall continue to or persistently violate this Code in regards to electrical
work, or the orders of the electrical inspector in relation to same, the
registration and permit of such person shall be suspended or revoked. (2014
Code § 5-305)
      2.   This Code shall not be construed to relieve or lessen the
responsibility of any person, partnership or corporation owning or operating or
installing electric wire, appliances, apparatus, construction or equipment for
the damage to property or persons injured by any defect therein. Nor shall the
Town or any agent thereof be deemed to assume such liability by reason of the
inspection authorized herein or the certificate of inspection issued by the
electrical inspector. (2014 Code § 5-306)
10-4-3: INSPECTION FEE:
The Town Board of Trustees, by motion or resolution, may prescribe an
inspection fee to be paid to the Town when electrical installations are
inspected by the electrical inspector. (2014 Code § 5-303)
10-4-4: UTILITY CONNECTION REQUIREMENTS:
It shall be unlawful for any electric light and power company or any supplier
of electricity for light, heat or power to make any electrical connection to
any building for electric wiring or apparatus until a certificate stating that
the electric work has been approved or written permit authorizing connection
has been issued by the electrical inspector. All firms, corporations or
individuals, whether operating under a regular franchise granted by the Town or
not, shall, upon written notice by the electrical inspector, disconnect from
any such circuit, including main service wires, branch feeder wires or
distribution, as designated by the notice, and shall not reconnect to the
installation except upon written notice from the electrical inspector. (2014
Code § 5-304)
10-4-5: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
A violation of this chapter shall be deemed a misdemeanor and shall be
punishable by fine. Any person, firm, or corporation who violates or refuses to
comply with any of the provisions of this chapter shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2014 Code § 5-307)
CHAPTER 5
MECHANICAL CODE AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
10-5-1: Mechanical Code

10-5-1: MECHANICAL CODE:
   A.   Adoption Of Code: The BOCA National Mechanical Code, the latest version
thereof, as published by the Building Officials and Code Administrators
International, Inc., is hereby adopted as the Mechanical Code of the Town for
the control of buildings and structures as therein provided. Each and all of
the regulations, provisions, penalties, conditions and terms of the Mechanical
Code are hereby referred to, adopted, incorporated and made a part hereof, as
if fully set out in this subsection, with the additions, insertions, deletions
and changes, if any, prescribed in subsection B of this section. At least one
copy of the Code is kept on file in the Town Clerk-Treasurer's Office. (2014
Code § 5-701)
   B.   Amendments To Code: The following sections of the Town Mechanical Code
are hereby revised as follows:
Insert: Town of Locust Grove.
Insert: Applicable fees shall be set by the Town by motion or resolution.
Insert: Offenses are punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of the Town Code.
(2014 Code § 5-702)
10-5-2: MECHANICAL CONTRACTORS:
   A.   State License And Town Registration Required:
      1.   No person shall practice or engage in the business, trade or
occupation of a mechanical contractor or a mechanical journeyman unless he has
a current and valid license issued by the State. Mechanical apprentices require
State registration. (2014 Code § 5-703; amd. 2018 Code)
      2.   No person shall practice or engage in the business, trade or
occupation of a mechanical contractor, a mechanical journeyman or a mechanic's
apprentice unless he has first registered as such with the Town and paid the
annual fee set by the Town Board by motion or resolution.
   B.   Bond And Insurance Requirements: Bond and insurance requirements of
mechanical contractors shall meet the requirements established by State law.
(2014 Code § 5-703)
10-5-3: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
A violation of this chapter shall be deemed a misdemeanor and shall be
punishable by fine. Any person, firm or corporation who violates or refuses to
comply with any of the provisions of this chapter shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2014 Code § 5-704)
CHAPTER 6
GAS REGULATIONS
SECTION:
10-6-1: Gas Piping
10-6-2: Liquefied Petroleum Gas Regulations Adopted
10-6-3: Violation; Penalty
10-6-1: GAS PIPING:
   A.   Code Adopted: The National Fuel Gas Code, as issued by the National
Fire Protection Association, the latest edition thereof, is hereby adopted,
incorporated and made a part hereof as if fully set out in this subsection,
with the insertions, deletions and changes if any prescribed herein. State
licensed plumbing and mechanical contractors and persons authorized to install
gas piping under State licensing laws are authorized to do so under this Code.
A copy of the Code is on file in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer for
public use and inspection. (2014 Code § 5-401; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Gas Piping Contractors:
      1.   State License Required: It is unlawful for any person to engage in
the business of installing gas piping or gas appliances without first obtaining
any license required by the State.
      2.   Bond And Insurance Requirements: Bond and insurance shall be
provided by the licensee in such amounts as required by the State. (2014 Code §
5-402)
10-6-2: LIQUEFIED PETROLEUM GAS REGULATIONS ADOPTED:
The National Fire Protection Association pamphlet no. 58 entitled "Storage and
Handling of Liquefied Petroleum Gases", also adopted by the Oklahoma Liquefied
Petroleum Gas Board, is adopted and incorporated herein by reference and shall
have full force and effect within the Town. A copy of the pamphlet is on file
in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer for public use and inspection.
   A.   Definitions: The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this
article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where
the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
INSPECTOR: The code enforcement officer, the building inspector, or the person
designated by the Board of Trustees to enforce this section.
LP-GAS SAFETY RULES: The rules adopted by the Oklahoma Liquified Petroleum and
Gas Board pursuant to 52 O.S. 420 et seq including any National Fire Protection
Association (NFPA) or other documents adopted by reference, as amended from
time to time.
NUISANCE PROPANE TANK: A propane tank that:
      1.   Has been determined by the inspector to be a danger to the public
health, safety, or welfare, not maintained in good working order or according
to the LP-gas safety rules, or not utilized safely or according to the LP-gas
safety rules or manufacturer's instructions;
      2.   Notice has been given of said determination pursuant to paragraph E
herein; and
      3.   The propane tank has not been remedied pursuant to the terms of the
notice within the time prescribed in paragraph E herein.
PROPANE TANK: An external, above-ground tank that stores an alternate fuel
source to natural gas used primarily for in-home or commercial cooking or
heating homes or businesses.
   B.   Propane Tanks Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for a person to use a
propane tank or a nuisance propane tank within the town limits or possess a
propane tank or nuisance propane tank for the purpose of use within the town
limits, except as provided herein.
   C.   Exceptions: A person may use a propane tank within the town limits if:
      1.   The propane tank was in active use within the town limits as of the
effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived and remains
on the property where the propane tank was located as of the effective date of
the ordinance from which this article is derived; or
      2.   A waiver has been granted as provided in the ordinance from which
this article is derived for use of the propane tank on the property specified
in the waiver, provided that the propane tank is located on the property
specified in the waiver and in active use.
   D.   Registration; Fee:
      1.   Any person possessing or using a propane tank within the town limits
under one of the exceptions in paragraph C above shall register the propane
tank with the town.
      2.   A person who was actively using a propane tank within the town
limits as of the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is
derived shall register the propane tank within six (6) months of the effective
date of the ordinance from which this article is derived and shall not be
required to pay registration fee during the six (6) month period.
      3.   A person who has been granted a waiver shall register the propane
tank within ten (10) business days of the waiver being granted.
      4.   A person who purchases a property upon which a propane tank is
located and actively uses the propane tank shall register as the new owner of
the propane tank within one (1) month of purchasing the property.
      5.   A person required to register under this section shall provide the
town with the address where the propane tank is located, the name of the person
who owns or is leasing the propane tank, and the name, address, and telephone
number of the company, if any, leasing the propane tank.
      6.   The registration fee shall be ten dollars ($10.00). If a person does
not register within the time prescribed herein, the person shall incur a late
fee of five dollars ($5.00).
   E.   Nuisance Propane Tanks:
      1.   A propane tank that constitutes a danger to the public health,
safety, or welfare, is not being maintained in good working order or according
to the LP-gas safety rules or is not being utilized safely or according to the
LP-gas safety rules or the manufacturer's instructions, is hereby declared to
be a nuisance.
      2.   If the inspector determines that a propane tank is a nuisance, the
inspector may issue written notice requiring that the person who owns,
possesses, keeps or uses the propane tank meet certain remedial requirements to
correct the danger posed by the propane tank. The notice shall be given to the
person who owns, possesses, keeps or uses the propane tank and to the company,
if any, leasing the propane tank by personal service, by posting notice at the
property where the propane tank is located, or by certified mail, return
receipt requested. The person shall have seven (7) days to comply with the
notice. The person may file a written appeal to this notice clearly stating the
reasons for the appeal, to the Board of Trustees within seven (7) days of
service. The Trustees shall conduct a hearing to determine the issues stated in
the written appeal. The decision of the Trustees shall be rendered within
thirty (30) days of the hearing.
      3.   If the inspector determines that the propane tank constitutes an
immediate danger to the public health, safety or welfare, the inspector shall
take such action as is reasonable and necessary to protect the public health
and safety, including immediately declaring the propane tank to be a nuisance
tank and/or seizing the propane tank.
      4.   If the person fails to comply with the notice or appeals the
decision within seven (7) days, the person shall deliver the propane tank to
the public works department located at 6939 S 440 Rd, Locust Grove, Oklahoma.
If the person fails to deliver the propane tank to the public works department,
the inspector may seize the propane tank.
      5.   Nothing herein precludes the town from seeking other remedies if a
person fails to comply with the remedial requirements stated or the decisions
rendered in the appeal process.
   F.   Waiver; Fee:
      1.   A person who wishes to own, possess, keep or use a propane tank
within the town limits may apply for a waiver from the town clerk.
      2.   A waiver may be granted only if gas service is unavailable to the
property for which the person is requesting the waiver. For the purposes of
this article, gas services shall be deemed unavailable if the nearest gas main
is located more than two hundred (200) feet from the nearest property line or
boundary of the property for which the waiver is being requested.
      3.   Any person who is denied a waiver may file a written appeal clearly
stating the reasons for the appeal to the Board of Trustees within ten (10)
days of the denial of the waiver. The Trustees shall conduct a hearing to
determine the issues stated in the written appeal. A decision of the Trustees
shall be rendered within fifteen (15) days from receipt of the appeal.
      4.   A person who is granted a waiver from the Board of Trustees shall
maintain the propane tank in good working condition or according to the LP-gas
safety rules, utilize the propane tank safely or according to the LP-gas safety
rules of the manufacturer's instructions, and ensure that the propane tank is
not a danger to the public health, safety or welfare.
      5.   The fee for applying for a waiver shall be ten dollars ($10.00). A
person granted a waiver shall be required to register the propane tank pursuant
to paragraph D above.
   G.   Location Of Propane Tank:
      1.   Propane tanks installed after the effective date of the ordinance
from which this article is derived shall not be placed within ten (10) feet for
one hundred twenty-five to five hundred (125 - 500) gallon tanks, and at least
twenty- five (25) feet for more than five hundred (500) gallons, of any
boundary or property line of the lot, tract or parcel of land on which the
propane tank is located.
      2.   Propane tanks that are relocated within the boundaries of a lot,
tract, or parcel of land shall be located in accordance with tank size as
stated this section.
   H.   Penalty For Violation Of This Section: The penalty for violation of
this section shall be in accordance with the penalty provision contained in
Section
1-4-1 of the Code of Ordinances. Each continuing day's violation under this
section shall constitute a separate offense. (2014 Code § 5-501; amd. 2018
Code; Ord. 2024-01, 2-19-2024)
10-6-3: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
A violation of this chapter shall be deemed a misdemeanor and shall be
punishable by fine. Any person, firm or corporation who violates or refuses to
comply with any of the provisions of this chapter shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2014 Code §§ 5-403, 5-502)
CHAPTER 7
FIRE CODES AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
10-7-1: Adoption Of Codes
10-7-2: Limits For Storage Of Flammable Liquids, Liquefied Petroleum Gas And
Explosives
10-7-3: New Materials, Processes Or Occupancies; Permits
10-7-4: Authority To Modify Regulations
10-7-5: Appeals
10-7-6: Penalties
10-7-1: ADOPTION OF CODES:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of prescribing regulations governing
conditions hazardous to life and property from fire or explosion, that certain
Code known as Fire Prevention Code recommended by the National Fire Protection
Association, and that certain Code known as the Life Safety Code recommended by
the National Fire Protection Association, being particularly the latest
editions thereof and the whole thereof, save and except such portions as are
hereinafter deleted, modified, or amended by this chapter. At least one copy of
the Fire Prevention Code and the Life Safety Code are on file in the Office of
the Town Clerk-Treasurer. The Fire Prevention Code and the Life Safety Code are
hereby adopted and incorporated as fully as if set out at length herein, and
from the effective date hereof, the provisions thereof shall be controlling
within the limits of the Town. (2014 Code § 13-101)
10-7-2: LIMITS FOR STORAGE OF FLAMMABLE LIQUIDS, LIQUEFIED PETROLEUM GAS AND
EXPLOSIVES:
The Town limits are the limits in the Fire Prevention Code in which storage of
flammable liquids in aboveground tanks, new bulk plants for flammable liquids,
bulk storage of LPG and storage of explosives and blasting agents are
prohibited. (2014 Code § 13-102)
10-7-3: NEW MATERIALS, PROCESSES OR OCCUPANCIES; PERMITS:
The Town Board of Trustees may act as a committee to determine and specify,
after giving affected persons an opportunity to be heard, any new materials,
processes, or occupancies, which shall require permits, in addition to those
now enumerated in the Codes adopted herein. The Fire Chief shall post such list
in a conspicuous place in his office and distribute copies thereof to
interested persons. (2014 Code § 13-103)
10-7-4: AUTHORITY TO MODIFY REGULATIONS:
The Town Board of Trustees shall have the power to modify any of the provisions
of the Fire Prevention Code and the Life Safety Code upon application in
writing by the owner or lessee, or his duly authorized agent, when there are
practical difficulties in the way of carrying out the strict letter of the
Codes; provided, that the spirit of the Codes shall be observed, public safety
secured, and substantial justice done. The particulars of such modification,
when granted or allowed, and the decision of the Fire Chief and Board of
Trustees thereon, shall be entered upon the records of the Board of Trustees,
and a signed copy shall be furnished the applicant. (2014 Code § 13-102)
10-7-5: APPEALS:
Whenever the Chief of the Fire Department shall disapprove an application or
refuse to grant a permit applied for, or when it is claimed that the provisions
of the Codes adopted herein do not apply or that the true intent and meaning of
the Codes have been misconstrued or wrongly interpreted, the applicant may
appeal from the decision of the Chief of the Fire Department to the Town Board
of Trustees within thirty (30) days from the date of the decision appealed.
(2014 Code § 13- 104)
10-7-6: PENALTIES:
Any person, firm or corporation who violates any of the provisions of the Codes
hereby adopted or fails to comply therewith, or who violates or fails to comply
with any order made thereunder, or who builds in violation of any detailed
statement of specifications or plans submitted and approved thereunder, or any
certificate or permit issued thereunder, and from which no appeal has been
taken, or who fails to comply with such an order as affirmed or modified by the
Town Board of Trustees or by a court of competent jurisdiction, within the time
fixed therein, shall severally for every such violation and noncompliance
respectively, be guilty of an offense, punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. The imposition of one penalty for any violation shall not
excuse the violation or permit it to continue, and all such persons shall be
required to correct or remedy such violations or defects within a reasonable
time. When not otherwise specified, each ten (10) days that prohibited
conditions are maintained shall constitute a separate offense. The application
of the penalty shall not be held to prevent the enforced removal of prohibited
conditions. (2014 Code § 13-105)
CHAPTER 8
PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE
SECTION:
10-8-1: Adoption Of Code
10-8-2: Appeals
10-8-3: Conflicting Provisions
