following the date of issuance. Application for renewal of permits may be made
within thirty (30) days prior to expiration at a fee set by the Town Board of
Trustees for the period of one year from the date of expiration.
   D.   Display Of Permit: The permit must be conspicuously displayed at all
times. (2014 Code § 12-206)
11-1-8: MOBILE HOMES OUTSIDE OF MOBILE HOME PARKS:
   A.   Parking On Public Ways: It shall be unlawful within the limits of the
Town for any person to park any mobile home of any kind on any street, alley,
highway or other public place in the Town.
   B.   Temporary Storage On Private Property: Temporary storage of unoccupied
mobile homes on private property may be permitted for a period of forty eight
(48) hours by obtaining from the Town Clerk-Treasurer a permit therefor by
filing an application describing the premises on which the temporary storage
will take place, duly signed by the record owner of such real property and
endorsed by the owner of the mobile home stand stating that he understands that
the permit is of a temporary nature and upon the payment of the fee as set by
the Board of Trustees to the Town Clerk-Treasurer for the issuance of such
permit, the Town Clerk-Treasurer shall issue said permit, which shall be
attached in a conspicuous place upon said mobile home. Failure to obtain or
attach such permit in a conspicuous place upon said mobile home constitutes an
offense.
   C.   Zoning Clearance Permit Required: Except for temporary storage, as
defined in subsection B of this section, or a permitted mobile home sales or
service establishment for the purpose of sales or service, or within an
approved mobile home park, no mobile home shall be parked, used or occupied on
any tract of ground in the Town without a zoning clearance permit as required
in this chapter.
   D.   Penalty:
      1.   The parking, usage, occupying or storage of any mobile home contrary
to the provisions of this section shall subject the owner to a penalty by fine
as provided in section
11-1-10 of this chapter, and each day shall be considered a separate offense.
      2.   The sufferance of an unauthorized parking of any mobile home by the
owner of any real property shall subject said owner to the same penalty as set
forth in subsection D1 of this section. (2014 Code § 12-206)
11-1-9: NONCONFORMING STRUCTURES AND USES:
   A.   Continuance Of Structure Or Use: Any building, structure or use
lawfully existing at the effective date hereof may be continued, even though
such building, structure or use does not conform with the provisions of this
chapter.
   B.   Damage To Structures: If any nonconforming building, structure, use or
mobile home is damaged by fire or natural disaster, such nonconforming use or
structure shall not be reerected or reestablished without the expressed consent
of the Board of Trustees who will consider and approve such request only if the
applicant can identify a hardship that was not self-imposed. (2014 Code § 12-
207)
11-1-10: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person, firm, association, corporation or copartnership who shall violate
any of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of an offense and,
upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. A separate offense shall be deemed committed upon each day
during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (2014 Code § 12-208; amd.
2018 Code)
11-1-11: ACCESSORY STRUCTURES:
Definition: RESIDENTIAL ACCESSORY STRUCTURE: Includes, but is not limited to,
accessory dwelling unit (ADU), barns, carports, decks, fences, flagpoles, play
houses, storage buildings, safe rooms, swimming pools, tree houses, and
workshops.
   A.   Generally Applicable Regulations:
      1.   Accessory Uses Allowed: Accessory uses and structures are allowed
only in connection with lawfully established principal uses.
      2.   Allowed Uses And Structures: Allowed uses and structures are limited
to those expressly regulated in this chapter as well as those that, in the
determination of the Board of Trustees, satisfy all the following criteria:
         a.   They are customarily found in conjunction with the subject
principal use or principal structure;
         b.   They are subordinate and clearly incidental to the principal use
of the property; and
         c.   They serve a necessary function for or contribute to the comfort,
safety or convenience of the occupants of the principal use.
      3.   Time Of Construction And Establishment:
         a.   Accessory uses may be established only after the principal use of
the property is in place.
         b.   Accessory buildings may be established in conjunction with or
after the principal building or use. They may not be established before the
principal building or use is in place.
      4.   Location: Accessory uses and structures must be located on the same
lot as the principal use to which they are accessory, unless otherwise
expressly stated.
      5.   Compliance With Lot And Building Regulations: Unless otherwise
expressly stated, accessory uses and structures are subject to the same lot and
building regulations as apply to principal uses and buildings.
      6.   Accessory Building Size: The total aggregate floor area of all
detached accessory buildings, including accessory dwelling units, and accessory
buildings not erected as an integral part of the principal residential building
may not exceed five hundred (500) square feet or forty percent (40%) of the
floor area of the principal residential structure, whichever is greater.
      7.   Permit: A permit is required for all accessory buildings regardless
of size of the building. This is to ensure that accessory buildings are not
placed over building setback lines or over utility easements or in a floodway
or floodplain.
         a.   Requirements For A Permit For Accessory Building:
            1)   The name of property owner, name of applicant, name of
contractor, if any, and the address or location of the proposed structure.
            2)   Description of the proposed structure providing details of
construction, components and proposed attachments to the ground or other basis.
            3)   Plot plan, in a scale of one (1) inch equals twenty (20) feet,
showing the boundaries of the property on which emplacement is proposed, the
precise location of the structure to all buildings and other structures on the
property, and to the property lines (plot plan example in Town Clerk's office).
            4)   For structures which contain or involve electrical wiring, a
plan in the form prescribed by the National Electric Code as adopted by the
town, giving all information required.
            5)   Mechanical/plumbing plans are required for any accessory
structure as prescribed by the Oklahoma Unified Building Code as adopted by the
town, giving all information required.
            6)   Permit fee(s) for an accessory structure.
      8.   Permit Review Process For Accessory Building: Applicants should
submit construction documents at least three (3) weeks before a building permit
is desired. Applicants will be notified after the plans have been reviewed by
the building inspector. Permits are valid for six (6) months; however, if a
relevant inspection has been approved within the first six (6) months, the
permit shall then be valid for a year from the date of issuance. The Board of
Trustees discourages applicants from ordering building materials or scheduling
labor prior to the issuance of a building permit.
      The owner or his/her authorized agent is responsible for coordinating all
required inspections after the permit is issued. Inspections are necessary
prior to covering any electrical, mechanical, plumbing or structural system
component. Inspections must be requested at least one (1) working day in
advance of when it is needed, and only the contractor of record can call for
their own inspections.
   B.   Residential Storage Buildings: In addition to other applicable
regulations, the following basic standards apply for accessory buildings:
      1.   Residential accessory buildings, such as detached garages, workshops
and storage buildings, that are to have three hundred fifty (350) square feet
or larger shall have a floor of concrete with a foundation which complies with
the building code.
      2.   Accessory structures shall not exceed eight (8) feet above the
ground in height at the wall, and the roof of said structure shall have a
minimum of 5/12 and a maximum of 12/12 roof pitch. These pitch requirements may
be waived for very small buildings that are prefabricated and intended as
temporary improvements.
      3.   Accessory, temporary and portable buildings, not including detached
garages that do not exceed two hundred fifty (250) square feet in area, shall
be exempt from requirements regarding footings and floors, but shall be
anchored in a manner approved by the building official that is at least
equivalent to using thirty-inch-long, double-helix anchors with steel bands
spaced sixteen (16) inches on center or at each end of the building.
   C.   Portable Storage Containers: Portable storage containers are not to be
used as permanent accessory structures. Placement of portable storage
containers is permissible for up to thirty (30) days, provided that an
appropriate permit has been obtained. Extension of this time is permissible
only in case of significant remodeling to the primary structure, in which case
the building inspector may extend the time to match the expiration of the
permit. Container placement shall not cause damage to landscaping. No container
shall be placed within the street right-of-way.
   D.   Safe Rooms:
      1.   In general, above and below ground safe rooms shall comply with
standards promulgated by the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) for
residential or commercial safe rooms. All plans and specifications submitted
for approval must meet the design requirements currently promulgated by FEMA.
      2.   Permit: No person shall install or modify a safe room without first
obtaining a safe room permit and paying the permit fee.
      3.   Location: Front yard locations are not permitted except when
location in the rear or side yard is not practical. Safe rooms installed in
front of the front building line shall comply with the following restrictions:
         a.   The top of the structure shall not extend more than three (3)
inches above finished grade. Structures exceeding three (3) inches above grade
but less than four and one-half (4-1/2) inches above grade may be approved at
the sole discretion of the building inspector and only if adequate landscape
screening is provided.
         b.   Vent pipes shall not extend more than twelve (12) inches above
finished grade.
         c.   Entrance ways must be provided with an external locking device,
such as a hasp and padlock.
         d.   Additional mitigation, including landscaping, may be required.
   E.   Accessory Dwelling Unit (ADU): Accessory dwelling units are allowed in
certain situations to:
      1.   Purpose And Intent:
         a.   Support more efficient use of existing housing stock and
infrastructure;
         b.   Provide housing that responds to changing family needs, smaller
households, and increasing housing costs; and
         c.   Provide accessible housing for seniors and persons with
disabilities.
      2.   Definition: A DWELLING UNIT (ADU) is a smaller, secondary home on
the same lot as a detached primary dwelling. ADUs are independently habitable
and provide the basic requirements of shelter, heating, cooking, and
sanitation. There are two (2) types of ADUs:
         a.   Accessory apartments are attached to or part of the primary
dwelling. Examples may include converted living space, attached garages,
basements or attics, additions, or a combination thereof.
         b.   Accessory cottages are detached structures. Examples include
converted garages or new construction.
      3.   Number: One (1) ADU is permitted per residential lot.
      4.   Creation: An ADU may be created through new construction, conversion
of an existing structure, addition to an existing structure, or conversion of a
qualifying existing house to an accessory cottage while simultaneously
constructing a new primary dwelling on the site.
      5.   Approval: The building inspector must approve the proposed ADU as
complying with the standards of this section. Applications for ADUs must meet
the following criteria:
         a.   The applicant must demonstrate that the ADU complies with all
development and design standards of this section; and
         b.   The applicant must demonstrate that the proposed modifications
comply with applicable building and fire safety codes.
      6.   Design: Design standards for ADUs are stated in this section. If not
addressed in this section, base zone development standards apply. All ADUs
(accessory apartments and accessory cottages) must meet the following
requirements:
         a.   Size: An ADU must be no more than seven hundred fifty (750) sq.
ft. or forty percent (40%) of the floor area of the principal residential
structure, whichever is greater.
         b.   Parking: No additional parking is required for an ADU. The
existing required parking for the primary dwelling must be maintained or
replaced on-site.
      7.   Building And Fire Codes: All accessory dwelling units are subject to
applicable building and fire codes.
      8.   Entrances: Building entrances to ADUs may not face the nearest side
or rear property line unless there is an alley abutting that property line.
      9.   Roof Pitch: The roof pitch of any new accessory dwelling unit must
be the same as the predominant roof pitch of the principal building.
   F.   Violations, Remedies:
      1.   When, in the opinion of the building inspector, any structure
permitted under this division is found to be in a condition which indicates
noncompliance with the provisions of this chapter or any other chapter of this
code, then in that event the town shall notify the permittee in writing of such
defect, giving permittee fifteen (15) days from the date of notification to
correct the noted deficiencies. If, at the expiration of said fifteen (15)
days, noncompliance still exists, then the town may seek revocation of any
permit by action of the Board of Trustees at a regularly scheduled Board of
Trustees meeting, the date and time of which shall be provided the permittee by
certified or registered mail. If the Board of Trustees finds, based upon the
town's and permittee's evidence, that any noncompliance exists, then the Board
of Trustees may order any corrective action deemed appropriate under the
circumstances. Should the permittee fail to comply with the directions of the
Board of Trustees, or if the Board of Trustees should find the condition to be
a hazard to life or property, then the Board of Trustees may declare same as a
public nuisance and order abatement as in the manner of law provided for the
abatement of public nuisances in the Town Code of Ordinances.
      2.   In addition, any person guilty of the violation of any of the
provisions of this article, upon conviction thereof, may be punished as
provided in Section
1-4-1 of the Locust Grove Code of Ordinances. (Ord. 2024-02, 2-19-2024)
